Many times they come in papers as things that look like hail in their shape and hardness, and because of this the disease is called 'hailstone'. It is an accumulation of moisture, thick on the paper above and below; the treatment is as follows: if the hailstone does not move from one side to another, and it is a minor issue, then it is easy to understand. Open it with tweezers, then peel it gently from each side; if you cannot cover it without piercing the paper, it will not harm the patient. If the tear is large, there should be a stitch, and the wound treated until it is healed; but if it is small, no force should be used, as the ointment will restore it immediately and prevent infection.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hematoma is descending within the ear towards the upper part, reverse the paper, and press it with pincers; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it does not matter; and when the hematoma is pressed, wash the eye with salty water, and cure the place of that which causes infection until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinac is a fat which is woven into webs of paper above, and this happens most to children with no people, and it hurts them a lot, and the catarrh comes to them in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes; and because of this, they lie on their faces, sleep on top, and have moist eyelids that are swollen and covered by the appearance of the exinac which opens in the eye. And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exnac coming out between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the operation is that the patient puts his head on yours; and then take .i. linen cloth, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that exnac contains in each part, and then put it on him; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the exnac is brought together within the circle; then make an incision in the middle of the moisture with a spatulum, making it no larger than the wound made for bleeding; and in various dispositions, exnac comes out of the incision according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take therefore a piece of cloth and hold it between your fingers and thumb, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to push into the fissure so that you do not go all the way to the sphincter muscle up to the eye and injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the external orifice opens at the beginning of the fissure, gently dilate the opening slightly so that it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten the cloth in vinegar and water, place it on the area, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are men who grind the area and apply something to corrupt the moisture that remains; then treat it until it is healed. And if a hot abscess comes to the area, treat it with soothing poultices until it is healed.Et s’il vient au leu aposteme freddure, si met sus emplaustre chaut tant qu’il est chaud; puis li met sus dous oile, et li cure de bendelz.
des poilz des papieres	And if a cold abscess comes to the area, apply a hot poultice until it is warm; then apply warm oil, and treat it with bandages.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow from papers that are different from nature, and they are enveillit, they harm themselves and cause various diseases, such as tears, softening of the papers, and albugine, leading to the destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways to treat this: either by cauterization with fire, or by using a medicine applied directly to the eye, or through incision and suturing, or via canes, depending on what I will describe.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the affected eye paper towards your left hand; if it is cured, that is good; otherwise, insert a needle with thread through the edge of the paper where the hair is growing, and pierce 1 thread through the upper part of the paper all the way to the edge, then turn the paper over and make an incision in the part under the paper, under the abnormal hairs, up to the sphenoid bone, following the path of the tear duct from the large lachrymal gland to the small one; then remove the thread and place a small tent made of cotton and linen underneath the paper, then draw a figure of eight on the paper, like a myrtle leaf, but the shape should depend on how much you see the divided paper rising.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is a need to cut out a large amount of paper according to how soft the paper is, then make an incision along the two lines you have marked, starting from the large lachrymal gland up to the small one; and let one of the incisions be close to the normal hairs in the thickness of a hair root, then insert the needle into one of the corners of the wound, then cut off all the skin; then bring together the two edges with a single stitch using an aiguille and fine woolen thread, and wipe away any blood, and allow the excess threads on the eyelids to dry for a while if you wish, or else cut them off, then leave the stitches in place for 3-4 days; then treat the wound without stitches using drying and constricting remedies, for the paper will heal quickly once the wound is closed and the edges brought together, but stitches are painful (as the ancients say), and this method is performed without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if there is another way: and it is that you draw the paper in the form of a figure which is like the myrtle leaf, as we have described, with .iiij. notches made according to the shape which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut out what is above with small scissors evenly according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with which to sew up the figure, and take another thread through the large pore, and the second thread through the small one, and bring the threads together between your fingers evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin over which you have signed, as we have described, then bring together the two lips of the wound by suturing, and heal it until it is healthy; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	and sometimes the hair of the paper is reversed; so you should use what we have said about the incision, but the suturing in one and the other is more artful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of warts is as follows: convert the parchment and insert it according to what I have said, then make two warts by skill, and two fine threads as long as the width of the sputum and the broad part; then tie two threads at both ends where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other skillfully above what is on top of the parchment of the eye, and strain the two warts from the two formed parts; and leave it thus for several days, and the skin that is strained will die and shrivel up and fall off when it dries.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is slow to heal, then treat the wart until it is healed; and when the wound is closed and the parchment lifted, the hairs will no longer grow; and this is the form of the two warts that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the work is such that you prick with a fine needle, and thread it with a fine and soft silk thread; then assemble the threads and tie them skillfully, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then prepare in the case a fine silk thread, and tie the ends of the thread; then put the patient's head into your hand; and let it be in the sun so that the work is declared, for it is a subtle and minute work, then pierce the needle all the way through the parchment to the root of the hair, and draw it out through the parchment until it comes out with the natural hair; then thread the hair into the case, if there are one or two or three or more hairs; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come out through the case with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the wound is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then treat the wound underneath all the way to the root that you have assigned to it, until the wound comes out from above the opening and you see it through the eye; then treat the wound and the thread, and close the eye and let it be closed for 1 or 2 days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows over it; and if the hair is short, then accompany one long hair of the horse's tail, and let it grow with that one you leave it, until it is elongated and then release it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the eye's pus
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called 'alacrity' or the pus comes in the eye, there are two ways it happens: one natural and the other unnatural. And it happens suddenly from a wound, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way to treat it is that you split that soudure, and loosen its eyelids, and put in it tents of linen, and dress it until it is healed; and one must not use in its treatment things that dry and constrict. For if you do this, then the disease will return worse than before; but one should use soft things, such as fenugreek; and rosewater or altered and seeded, and daiquilon ointment melted in some of the oils, and wrap a tent around it, and treat it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you must take care that it does not heal according to its former shape; and these works which we have said are not remedies for this disease, but preventions so that it does not return to its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease which lies beneath the skin is truly called "axacrati", and it has natural and accidental causes. The accident comes from wounds, cuts, cautery, and similar things; and the way to treat it is to take a needle with .i. double thread, pierce the flesh at the outer corner of the eye so that the thread passes through both eyelids, then tie the thread tightly so that the eye is pulled up and the eyelid is opened wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the papery returns to what it should be, that is good; if not, take a razor and insert it into the slit, turn the paper over, and cut  .ij. slits along the sides within the paper; let the corners of the  .ij. slits where you inserted the thread be at  .i. angle so that when they are joined together, the shape is like the shape of a letter with the name " .j. griesche"; then remove the thread, according to the quantity that his sides are cut underneath, then attach the two separated parts and sew them together with a thread of wool; then treat it as we have said with softening medicines, and tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the disease comes from a split or a stitch or cautery, then one should make a plain slit underneath the hair of the scalp, and according to what is mentioned above; then unsheathe between the two lips of the tent, as I have said; and one must perform the operation according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters prepare remedies with all their might, so that they may bring the figure back to its natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what is needed in terms of treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the scalp
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suddenness happens to the scalp in such a way that the scalp above is separated from the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then one should insert the tip of a razor underneath the scalp, and lift it upward; and press it with tweezers, until you grab what is cut into the spatulum, which is neither too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient cannot bear the pain of the too-sharp spatulum cutting into the eye; and your incision, by which you peel back this membrane, should be light, so that the scalp returns to its natural shape; and all of this assembly is healed, and they sometimes produce a saline solution in the eye, and raise it with sweet water, and use a bandage; then place a tent made of linen between the scalp and the eye, and place soft wool soaked in egg yolk on top of the eye; and after the third day, use the ointment and soothing remedies until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the eyelid
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is in two ways: it is nervous and resembles a hard cyst, and another which is not nervous but resembles white congealed moisture; when touched by iron and pinched with tweezers, neither can be removed. Both appearances begin at the large tear duct, growing little by little until they cover the entire eye and its sight and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient tilts his head toward you, then he opens his eyes; and hold the paper in your hand, then grab the nail with tweezers and pull it up slightly; then take a needle and thread through a horse, cow or ox hair, and double the end of the needle over, then pierce the nail with the entire needle, and tie the nail with a string and tie it above, then scrape all along the side of the nail where the tear duct is, up to the eyebrow, leaving the natural skin around the tear duct, so that by the incision the tears do not come out as usual; sometimes the nail is just stuck on the needle and thread, as we have said; then scrape it off all along the tear duct gently and with small movements.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the tear duct does not touch the thread and break it, and that the eyelid is not pierced; after the incision, put a little powdered chalk in the eye, and make a collar of litargir, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as needed until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerved and you cannot push in the needle and the hook cannot enter, this kind of nail is often cured by medicines; they grow as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, then work the eye of the disease, and take the spatulum gently punctured according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And draw the nail gently, and if you see that it is not lessened and the reason approaches, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litarge and red copper and powdered chalk, and stop the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same action, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then milk it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then begin the work again as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid hurts the eye greatly, then suspend it on the hook, and cut off a part but not all so that the body of tears does not come in; then distill into the eye red collar made from litarge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows on the eyeball
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	In some people's eyes, red flesh sometimes grows over the eyeball, covering it and pressing down on the eyelids, and it looks like a rosebud; then the patient puts his head into your lap, and you work on the eye, and cut away all the flesh with suitable scissors, and hold it in place firmly; then cut away the first piece of flesh, and continue cutting carefully until it is all removed, being careful not to cut the eyeball while working on it. The incision should be made with a spatulum as described for the incision on a fingernail, using gentle force to remove the flesh, as demonstrated in this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Once the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, apply eye salve made of linseed oil mixed with red vitriol and other corrosive medicines; then cover the eye with a pad soaked in egg white to protect it from hot abscesses. If nothing remains, and the warm abscess becomes cold, and you still doubt that there is an abscess, leave the eye and treat the abscess with cooling remedies. Then return to your work on the eye until it is healed, and do the same for any other eyes with similar problems.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you should also know how to treat weak eyes by the natural way, and with surgery for accidental injuries; and do not insert your fingers in any of these procedures until you see that this member is suffering from that procedure.
des voines des eulz	of veins of them
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Red veins that are covered above the eye, and tolerate vision and weaken the eye all day. Therefore, first, you must examine the eye, because if it is in such a state, it is out, and there is no other disease except the red vein; then treat it in this way: instruct the patient to lower their head into your lap, then gently squeeze those veins at the edge according to his judgment, and let the edges be double according to this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two edges be gradual in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then treat the veins firmly, and draw out the blood drop by drop after another, until you see the veins removed from the eye; and be careful not to bruise the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not touch the veins; and when you have done this, distill into the eye a green and red collyrium to corrupt what remains of the vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to pull out all of them in that hour, then make a plaster over the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain is eased and there is assurance of a hot abscess, then begin again according to this method which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of strength:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The doctor should also examine the 'arissati' fistula: when you cure it with cautery and medicine that burns according to what I have said before, if it is not healed, then there must be a cut made over the abscess where it should remain, and all the moisture within must be drawn out until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, then it is necessary to use this instrument; and it is called an 'aspre chief', and it must be made from a very hard substance, with one end pointed like a file as shown in the present figure.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the site of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers and press your hand a little while until you know that the corruption has been removed; do this several times, then restore the site with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if the site is sewn up and there is no swelling and the body of the bow is sewn up and remains so for 40 days, and it does not open and no evil occurs, you know that it has healed; if not, then you must simply open the fistula at its opening with a knife according to this form: you uncover the bone a second time with an iron and with watery medications, and when it is uncovered, take up .i. forest according to this form, and let the head of the iron be pointed, and let the staff be thinned down to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone over the ulcer, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then bring back the whole forest until it pierces the bone and he feels it through his finger; then restore the site with dry medications as I have taught you, and when the scabs come out and harden the site, wash the matter off at the finger; this is an easier thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the output of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully open all around and do not disturb the nose or cause thinning, then you should ligate the patient; then cleanse the eye, then place leeches or suckers without piercing to draw out fluid; then apply a poultice made from acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla onto the eye; then tightly bind the eye with bandages and linen; the method for the linen is that you take quite soft linen, double each piece in four, then place one on top of the other according to how much the eye needs; then tightly bind it from above with a sturdy bandage, and repeat the leeches without piercing to draw out fluid; then remove the leeches and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the ligature becomes loose, you should re-bind it tightly; then remove the ligature after one day and one night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, then repeat the poultice, bandages, ligature, and leeches until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the rupture of a woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a tear occurs in woven fabric, it opens and reveals something like a grain of resin, which is frightening to see; therefore, if you see it covering, the work is such that you thread a needle into the root of the lower part up to the upper part, then thread another needle with a double thread through the part of the tear; and pierce it, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cover the area of the double thread and tie one part of the fabric tightly, then pull out the needle and place wet woolen cloth on the eye; and leave it until the threads tear with the fabric, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound heals; and sometimes the wound is constrained by the fabric on each side in a circle of cloth, until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes give great appearance, then pierce them with a thin spatulum which comes from the bottom of the eye, and scrape away the white moisture and bring the eyes down, and enter in immediately; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the corner of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but an inflammation which gathers in the eye, resembling descending water, but it is not water; and the appearance of its treatment is that you make the patient sit upright and still, then take his head in your hands from both sides and move him until you see the corner of the eye coming to the front of your eyes; then let it settle there, and don't let the light go away and have the patient see things as he used to; and if it doesn't go under, know that it is water, and if the corner of the eye isn't appearing as we have said, make the patient sit between your hands, then take a thin spatulum and press on the surface of the cornea with the conjunctiva and the corona until the water comes out; and when it is discharged, distill into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek that has been boiled and honey, then let it be treated with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the appearances of the diseases in the division, and what is necessary to pierce; then act according to health. You should make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light so as not to be affected by the sun, and tie up the healthy eye tightly; then place the paper over the eye, on your left hand if the eyes are on the left, or your right hand if they are on the right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are on the left, the instrument called 'almagda', or in your left hand if the eyes are on the right; then place the tip of the instrument alongside the crown by the thickness of a hair in that white part of the eye to the point where the tear duct is smallest, then push the instrument called 'almagda' skillfully, and turn your hand so that it pierces through the white of the eye, and feel that 'almagda' comes into the empty space; and the measure of the path of 'almagda' should be at the bottom of the space between the pupil and the edge of the iris; this is the crown of the eye; then you will see the bone in that paper due to the clarity of the horn-like tissue, and then place the instrument where the aqueous humor is, then express it beneath one pathway after another. If the aqueous humor flows out now, the patient can see in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, if the aqueous humor flows back up the second pathway, push it down with the instrument, and when it is firmly lodged and does not flow up again, gently remove 'almagda' by turning your hand a little; then put in a little more sealed oil gem, and leave it in the eye. Then place a soaked cotton or wool pad in rose oil and egg white on top of the eye, and tie it with the healthy eye. We, and those of our time, apply crushed comfrey with plenty of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if  'almagda' cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some people whose eyes are too hard, then you should take the instrument called  'alberit', which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a small slit, then put in almond milk, as we have said; and when the work is complete, prepare for the patient a dark room where he can sleep on his back in a dark place; and keep him still from all movements, and give him light food, and do not let him move his head or to the right or to the left, and tie him according to his condition until the third day; then untie him in that same dark room, and test his sight, and show him some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day; and you must not do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but you should lighten it, so that the water rises gently.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And if a hot abscess comes, you must untie the eye before the seventh day, and use what soothes the abscess; and when it is soothed, untie the sight and put on an eyelid cover to cover one eye, and then stay in that dark room. And then leave the house little by little, and return to his normal state; and know that no student should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Iraq, who told us that in his country they pierce and put almond milk into it, so that water is drawn out, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps this is a new thing.Et s’il vient a l’oil que le tenebros ne peut estre remedeiz par nullis de cestz chapitrez, que tu deslie la veue et la metes en son leu, car il ne se pourait mie remedeer.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the shapes of almagest , because those who do not know them will see them; and they are properly of iron:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the heads of the needles have this same subtlety, and the hindmost are pointed in three angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the eye through the nostril
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes, there are various types of growths that emerge from the nostrils, some of which resemble scorpions with multiple legs; and among these, there are those with a dark-colored swelling, and others with a light-colored lump. Therefore, for the latter type of growth, you should make the patient stand facing the sun, pinch his nose shut, pour the medication onto the growth, and pull it outwards; then, as far as you can endure it, use a delicate needle to pierce the growth from one side, until you are sure that the entire growth has been removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing which we cannot cover, then open it at all .i. of the subtle instruments slightly, so that nothing remains; and if without you are overwhelmed, or abscess bad, then dry it as it should be; and if it is malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize it until the blood is stained and all the flesh is removed, then pour or neat's milk and water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And if the ear works, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not break through as it should, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, because the instruments do not come to cut: therefore you must put into the ear a thread of linen about half a finger thick, and let it hang from the hand, and have between each knot a distance of one or two fingers; and let the patient hold the end of the thread in his mouth with all his strength, and draw it through until it comes out through the nose; and many children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for anyone who wants to do it; then hold the end that comes out of the nose in one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth in the other hand, and pull them gently towards you alternately while holding them steady. Do this until you know that the thread has corrupted the flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the ear as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh; and then put a plug of pitch in the nose for a few days until it is healthy, and if medicine is needed to dry it, then use it. This is the form of the instrument to clean the ear, with which one distils oils and medicines into the ear.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and it should have a handle to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid. And if you wish, make a closed cane, and let the instrument be hollow to clean out the ear; and have a plug in the ear to hold it while heating the oil or other liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart through the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises at the tip of the nose; it grows and becomes large until it is visible to the eye. Therefore, you should cut it at the beginning and remove all the pus; then apply fire cautery or burning medicine. If you delay cutting it until it becomes large, take care that it is not hard, of dark color, or insensate: do not touch it with iron, for this is a deep abscess. For when it is cut once, great harm comes to the patient. If the abscess is due to touch and not to dark color, and you see that it can be entirely covered, then empty the wound and cut it without fear, cleansing the area of dry and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should know that when pus comes from a broken cartilage, it does little good in some people. Therefore, whenever this happens to anyone, you should examine whether the wound is fresh and full of blood; then bring together the .ij. lips with one stitch, then cleanse it until it heals. If the lips are dislocated on both sides, you should scorch all the parts of their skin until they heal, then bring together the .ij. lips with a stitch, tighten them, and apply powdered dragon's blood and incense; place a piece of strong plaster or other binding plaster over the powders, leave it to dry by itself, then cleanse it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of sewing is that you prepare the thread: either with needles, as we have said in sewing the belly; or with a thread, as I have already informed you.
des apostemes des levres	of lip abscesses
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, there are hard abscesses inside the lips, resembling grains of wheat, smaller and larger; therefore, you must twist the lips, and slit them at each end, then grab them with tweezers and cut into each part; then apply vitriated quicklime to the incision until the blood is stanched; and then leave it with garlic, and treat the area with dry substances until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of gum swelling
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a growth arises on the gums, which the ancients call "albus"; you should hold it with tweezers, and cut at its root, and let the blood or pus run out; then apply powdered vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders, over the site. If the growth returns after the incision, and this often happens, cut it again, and cauterize it; if it does not return after the cautery, that is how you treat an abscess.
des sordens	from filth
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are growths at the base of the teeth, in the mouth between the gums, which are unsightly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, or green, due to corruption in the gums, and they smell bad; you should make the patient hold his jaw open and expose the teeth or gums, removing everything until it is clean; and thus you should treat blackness, yellowness, greenness, and other discoloration, until they are cleaned. If what was removed at first returns, it is good; if not, then do it again the next day and the day after, until everything is removed. Know that teeth require various types of instruments for cleaning, depending on what the job shows you, so that the instruments used to clean between the teeth have different forms from those used to clean the gums; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat a toothache that you delay pulling the tooth only as long as you can, because it should not be done; for it is a very serious matter to pull a tooth without cause.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore, when the patient is forced to pull, you must be certain about the tooth. Many times, the pain deceives the patient and thinks it is in the good tooth, and pulls out the good tooth; and yet the pain does not go away because of this, as long as the bad tooth remains, for we have already wanted to do this to these patients. And when you are certain about the tooth, you must scrape around the tooth all around strongly to push back the gum from all sides; then move it with your fingers or with small tweezers into the first pocket and pocket, until it is well loosened, then hold the tweezers firmly. And let the patient's head be between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	Then pull out the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take one of these instruments and insert it slightly into each side, and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is pierced and rotten, you must fill the holes with cotton, where the holes are; and then hold it firmly with tweezers so that it does not break when pulling; and you must work very gently around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to break it and leave a part of it, and bring back greater pain to the patient through the malice of the root than before. And beware that you do not do as the ignorant surgeons do, who often in their haste and arrogance break the tooth, and do not pay attention to what we have said; but sometimes they bring great illness through the holes made by the roots that remain, or by breaking the tooth, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine or garlic and vinegar; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, then apply powdered vitriol to the site; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, which make the teeth loose first, should have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be made of thick metal so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be well-made iron, and they should be toothed to grip the roots.
de la racine des dens	of the tooth roots
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains during pulling, you should put wet cotton on the area for one or two days, until the gums are softened. Then, use tweezers called "algefri", which make the gums look like a doctor's beak. They should be made inside like a file, and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tweezers, you must uncover the skin all around the root, and insert the instrument called "althali", that is, a spatula, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	Let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through it, that is good; if not, use all the instruments, whose shapes come later:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one can also use this instrument with .ij. fingers, whose shape is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools which are in front of the reason for the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large tweezers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	Let this instrument be so strong that it cannot break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise, subtle master finds his own instrument according to what his work and the illness show him, for there are many illnesses where the ancients did not teach an instrument because of the variety of causes. And if it does not break in the bone or in any of the other bones, but protrudes, then he searches for the instruments that he needs, which I have told you about, and helps with gestures, by which these are the forms:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-fitting to hold the bone, so that it does not slip but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with suitable medicines. And if there is a protuberance in the bone, and it is small, then treat it with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When a tooth appears not according to nature, and the shape is ugly, especially in young women, you should know whether the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in its proper place, and cannot be filed or ground down. Then pull it out; and if there is an air pocket with the tooth, take this instrument whose shape is like a small beak, and let it be made of iron with a pointed end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And tap it gently day by day because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others. And if it is apparent that it can be ground down, then grind it with a file like this, in the shape shown:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the lime that needles are made from; and with lime gently prick the tooth little by little day after day, so that it does not move until it falls out; then smooth it completely at the end with a file, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, file down the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front teeth loosen, by a blow or falling, and the patient cannot chew without spitting it out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines without success; then they must be restrained with a gold wire, because silver wires turn green and rust, but gold never moves; and the wire should not be too thin or too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth. And if you want to direct the teeth, take the wire and wrap it twice around the two healthy teeth, then place the loose tooth in between, whether there is one or more, so that you reach the bleeding to the healthy tooth on the other side. Then start covering again from where you began, and pull your hand gently and firmly, so that it does not move; and the ligature should be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then twist the wire with pliers, and assemble them, and reinsert them between the healthy tooth and the loose one, so that it does not cut the tongue; and then leave it tight as long as it can stay, and if it comes undone, or the wire breaks, then restrain it with another wire. It will stay like this all his life, and this is the shape of the teeth and the form of how to direct the two healthy teeth and the two loose ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, if one is put in its place, fresh after fresh, as we have said; and no one who is not wise and experienced should attempt this, and sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from a cow's bone, and it is put in the place where there is a defect, and it is restrained as we have said, and it stays and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	cut off the hair of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	At times this ligament comes from under the tongue as a birth defect, or it can result from an abscessed wound. The treatment is to open the mouth of the patient, tilt their head back, and lift up the tongue. Then cut the thick nervous ligament, making sure that the tongue is loosened from its socket. If there is any hardening due to an abscess, cut it open and treat the wound. Be careful not to cut too deeply into the artery underneath. Once you're finished, raise the affected area with a poultice of rosewater and garlic, or with cold water. Then place a tent made of linen under the tongue, and every night apply a blistering agent to the wound so that it doesn't heal closed. If there is any bleeding, apply crushed vitriol; if not, cauterize with a lentigo cautery, which is suitable for this purpose. Once the wound is healed, treat it with other treatments as needed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is black or hard and the patient doesn't feel any pain, then don't touch it, as it is likely a cancerous growth. If it is declining towards a blister and there is moisture, pierce it with a needle and release the fluid with a gentle spatulum, opening it from both sides. If bleeding occurs due to your intervention, apply crushed vitriol until it stops, then return to your treatment until all the pus is drained. Raise the affected area with poultices of garlic and salt, and treat the wound with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	from abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes bumps called "godath" appear in the throat, and they are properly called tonsils.
