When you treat them as described in the section on tonsillitis, and they do not heal, be careful: if they are hard abscesses of small size and a dark color, do not touch them with iron. If they are red and the root is thick, do not touch them with iron either, to prevent bleeding; but let them be until they rupture on their own. If they are white and the root is thin, prepare an instrument for cauterization, but first check that the abscesses have subsided and are calm. Then have the patient sit facing the sun, with his head tilted back, and the surgeon holding a piece of cloth between his teeth and pressing the tongue down under the instrument, which should be made of silver or thin brass like a small knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Then press the tongue down with the instrument and you will see the abscess. Take a pair of tweezers and grab it, pulling it out of the tonsil and up towards the surface as far as possible; pull some threads from the cloth along with it, then cover the instrument again, which should be shaped like a hook, to create a grip, and is made of either iron or copper.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument available, use tweezers, which should be shaped like a hook:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And it has a sharp point on one end and a flat edge on the other; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, cut the other in the same way, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, and with water and garlic, and if there is bleeding, gargle the patient with water, or with peels of pomegranates that have been cooked, or with myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses besides the two tonsils appear in the throat, so cut them thus as the two tonsils are cut.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, namely, one abscess of small size; and she had almost completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the opening which was blocked, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had stayed like that for one or two more days. And the abscesses had risen up so much that they had pushed two teeth out of their sockets. I hurried therefore at once, and made an incision in one of the openings, then removed a large amount of pus; then I made another cut in the other opening of the throat, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards, I inserted the knife into the abscesses, and cut out part of it, and only a little blood came out; thus the throat of the woman was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut that abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again, filling up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large; so I packed it with a poultice and cauterized it inside her throat; thus it stopped growing. And I left those parts, and did not know what happened to her afterwards.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the lens has descended into the pupil, and it is swollen and it is long, then it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thick and round beneath, then it is called an "uve." When it has been cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the coat of the abscess is pacified, and it is thin; and it is round and not long; and it is blood-red or yellow or black, then you should avoid cutting into it. For there is great danger in doing so. Therefore, when you see it, according to its whiteness and length, you should make the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument which we have mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the pupil, and draw it underneath, and cope with it using one of the two instruments which I mentioned for the incision of the two almond-shaped areas. And you must not cope beyond the natural limit, for if you do, it will harm his voice and speech. After the incision, use what we said about the incision of the two almond-shapes, and cure it until it is healed. And if the patient fears having it copped, then you should use a cautery on him without fear. The manner of cauterization is as follows: The patient puts his head on your healthy shoulder, and then presses his tongue against the instrument which we mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, and applies it with live coals so that they are not too thick or too hot; and use the tip of this instrument, whose shape is thus:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has a handle on its head where the medicine is placed, like the handle of a spoon, and you place the instrument with all the medicine on the pupil; and the patient lies on his side, so that the saliva and mucus from the medicine run out of his mouth and do not go down into his throat and lungs. Then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the pupil for the duration of half an hour, until you see it become numb and the bites of the medicine are pacified. And if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton on top, so that the cotton sticks to the pupil; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and remove it after four or five days. And if you need to renew the cautery with medicine, then renew it, and after the cautery, wash around the pupil with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine; and use a cold compress, and treat it with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery. If it is cured by fumigation according to this method, take calamin, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, wormwood, and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and add garlic, and let it boil; and the pot should be well glazed with strong earth, and in the pot there is one instrument with a handle shaped thus:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And be of silver or bronze, and put one of the heads into the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through the tube, until the eye is mortified; after that, repeat often, until the eye dries out, and beware that you do not do this at the beginning of the occurrence of a hot abscess, for many things happen then; and do not do this except at the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put inside it an egg-shell, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the egg-shell will not let the vapor burden the mouth, and this is a good and safe treatment.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or fish spine, or some object, gets stuck in the throat; so you must try to remove what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with the whole instrument, so that you can move the object; and if it does not come out and is lodged in the throat, you should make the patient vomit until the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a dry piece of bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches the spot, it will lodge there, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out in the way we have described, take an instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and let the head be raised upward; and beware of touching the epiglottis, lest it be torn, nor push the bone in; and move the patient's head so that he vomits, in order to dislodge the object; then he swallows the instrument, so that he can dislodge the object; if he cannot swallow it, then pull it out with the whole instrument, equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the saliva of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes the saliva is treated with medicine, as I have said in the classification, by applying remedies; and if this does not help, then examine the throat of the patient facing the sun, then press his tongue with the instrument I told you about. And if you see the saliva, pull it out with a small hook, or use fine tweezers that are suitable for this purpose. If this doesn't work, take a long needle and put it in the patient's throat, then heat the needle, and do this frequently. If the patient has a fever all day, take a glass of cold water, open his mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, moving his jaw often; as soon as the saliva feels the water, it will come out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it doesn't work as we have said, then smoke the patient's throat with assafetida, using the instrument I described for smoking the throat; do this many times, because it will work without delay. The method of smoking is to place burning charcoal in a pot with a perforated lid, and insert the tip of the instrument through the hole; then blow your smoke into the instrument, and have the patient put the needle in his mouth and close his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but reaches the saliva; the saliva will come out now, and if it doesn't work, then repeat the smoking many times. Let the patient be thirsty, and eat salted and sour foods, and drink no water; and then he will need to urinate.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to pull the saliva is, when you can see it, similar to curved tweezers that can enter the throat; it should be shaped like a surgeon's forceps, with roughness from lime so that it can grasp and not let go; here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	There are many types of abscesses, depending on their appearance, as the recollections in this book from various sources show, and they differ in how they are punctured and in their size. They occur in two ways: either according to their appearance or according to the location in the body. An abscess in the head is different from one in the fundament, and an abscess in fleshy tissue is different from one that occurs in joints, and each requires a different treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And in some abscesses, one must not puncture them until the pus is mature according to its completion; and there are some that one must puncture when they are mature, or they will not complete their digestion, as with those near joints. For when an abscess occurs near a joint, if you let it become purulent all around, the ligament and nerve of the joint may become corrupted, causing contraction in that limb. Or if the abscess is near the principal organ, if you delay piercing it until it is mature, it will harm the principal organ; or if it is near the fundament, one must pierce it so that it may mature; and one should not puncture a mature abscess before its digestion is complete, except for those near the fundament, which may become purulent and prolonged inside without causing fistula, and will heal in a reasonable time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And one should know the time of piercing an abscess that is mature according to its digestion, and it is when the pain has subsided, and the decrease in fever, and the lessening of swelling and redness, and the improvement in appetite and the appearance of pus; and one must pierce where the abscess is most dependent, and where there are signs of pus forming. And the piercing should be at a distance from the heart, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints affecting nerves and arteries, and in all places equally where there is no folding of the skin.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	Here, [you should] treat according to the affected member. And when an abscess is in fleshy tissue, it is best that you leave the puncture until it is fully healed and digested, as we have said. For if you pierce it earlier, it will lengthen the body from which the venom comes, and it will fill with filth; and the lips and depths of it may harden. And for some abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs. And one should treat small abscesses with small punctures, and large abscesses with large punctures, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses where one must pierce the heart, and cover it when it has become like a drape, and is deadened, one should do as one does with blisters. And there are some that are split into three angles, and some which are covered like the leaf of a bay tree, as with abscesses of the fingernails; and some where one makes a round incision, and other incisions, and similar covers.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those without a head, such as a superficial abscess, should be punctured directly; and when the abscess is large and has drawn a great deal of pus, one should not draw out all the pus at once, but only a portion; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more pus; do this repeatedly until all the pus comes out. This is especially important if the patient is weak, a woman, a small child, or an elderly person. For sometimes the pus will spurt out with the opening of the abscess and the patient may die from it without your realizing it. So be very cautious with this chapter; after you have punctured your abscess, wash the wound, and examine whether the wound of the abscess is small. If it is a plain incision, dress it with tents made of linen or old cotton; if it is a large abscess with many punctures, you should stuff each puncture with a tent so that they press against one another. If you have cut into the skin of the abscess and spread it open, then fill it with dry cotton or a lining of a linen dress without moisture, and leave it for three days; then remove it and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is bleeding from your work, then apply cold water and vinegar, and moisten a cloth, and place it over the bleeding area repeatedly. And if the bleeding continues, apply a regime and treatment, and the powders I have described earlier in this book; and if it is winter, and the area is very nervous, then you should place moistened tents and cloths that have been warmed in wine and hot oil over the area. If it is summer, and the area is fleshy, then moisten the cloths with water and oil, or cold wine and oil, for three days as we have said; then loosen the abscess, wash and treat it, as appropriate, until it is healed.Et se li apostemes est en leu nervouseux, si covient que tu mettes sus drapelz em aigue et vin, et oile, et l’eschaude, et ponses par maintes fois; et se c’est ou tens de l’iver, si mets sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en aigue chaude, et en vin chaut, et en oile; et se li leus est charnu, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz em aigue et vin froit, et en oile, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit.  Et puis deslie l’aposteme, et essue la plaie, et cure, si com il covient; et se li bowe est mout grant, si traie tentes derechief; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement, si com il covient tant qu’il soit sanez.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And so it is necessary to understand generally in the treatment of abscesses; now I have told you how one must go about treating abscesses, and see this chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Or of the head come small abscesses, and they are like those of people who are in cloth, like the jowls of a guinea-hen, and there are many similar ones. Some are fatty and some have pus; and there are some that are hard and stony in texture, and there is no doubt if the artery doesn't cause problems. The action of the jaw is such that you should test all instruments, called 'entromissoires', from which the form comes, whatever it contains. For if it contains moisture, then draw it out from above the long bone. And when the moisture has been drained, then scrape off the skin that contains the moisture, for it will heal as it dries; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is available; if not, in water and salt, and apply this to the wound and leave it until the next day, and then repeat with the cotton as before on the second and third days, until you are sure that it no longer contains any moisture; then treat the wound with suitable ointment until it heals. And if the abscess contains a hard knot, cut it according to the following form from above, and gouge out its roots, and scrape away all around it, and apply all your treatment to drawing out the pus from under the coat in which it lies; and if the artery causes problems, then do as I told you later. And also do this for an abscess that is stony, in terms of texture, and in terms of treating it, just as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the incision on a moist and stony abscess is easier, for they contain little blood. And there are some abscesses on the head where there is no moisture, and among these was one that I opened on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a pebble, rough and white, and could not be broken up; if anyone had cut it, they would have caused a wound like a stone. Other abscesses coming on the head, before those that come on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should be made as low as possible so that the pus can flow out; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes elsewhere in the body, and they are numerous, and are interconnected with each other. Each scrofula is properly located within its coat, as we have said for the vein and the abscess of the head; and there are many similarities among these scrofulas. Some contain moisture, and some are malignant and will not respond to treatment. So when you see one that has a good disposition, and resembles the color of the body, and is flat on each side, and is not adherent to the nerves of the neck, nor to the artery or duct, and is not deep; then you should cut it from above, and scrape away the skin from every part, and if necessary, you should use the two lips of the heart as we have described for abscesses in the head. Then gently pull it out bit by bit, being careful not to cut any nerve or vein, nor let the spatulum dig too deeply, so that the hand does not slip, and do not go too far ahead, so you don't cut anything you shouldn't.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it will not let you work on it, then put in the wound powdered glass, or some powder that stops bleeding, and tie off the wound; and leave it until the abscess is resolved, and the wound softens and begins to suppurate. And when the blood has clotted, return to your work, until you have finished it; then seek with your finger if there are any small scrofulas remaining, and cut and clean them. And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofula, then do not cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it off with a strong double thread, and let it hang by that; then treat the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you scrape all the scrofula, you should bring together the two lips of the wound and stitch them now, since there is no longer any surplus due to the size of the scrofula. Then you should attend to covering the root of it, pulling it out and stitching as we have said. For those scrofulae that hold a surplus, pierce where it appears dead; and pierce in the same way as the one previously mentioned, hanging a tent with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is clean, cure it with ointment mixed with charcoal until it is healed.
de squinance	of scrofula
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of cutting the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the written account of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with scrofula, it is necessary to cut the throat, which is called the "epiglottis"; and one should not make an incision through this, because all the veins and the lungs are affected by the disease in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the lungs, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to split the epiglottis, we must split it below three or four circles, or a small slit across, between two circles, or according to the amount of the slit in the soft palate; not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those places where it is suitable to split the epiglottis so that there is no cartilage, and the vessels are long within.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, he should extend the skin of the throat to the entire opening, then split the soft palate as far as the uvula; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then cover the soft palate as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and is demonstrated by the section of the blood vessel of the finger which jumped out through the place which is broken, and by the failure of the voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open a little.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed of which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the heart, and heal it all along without the cartilage; then administer remedies that promote healing, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely healed, and the patient is judged dead, and the lack of breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore, press on the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and for this the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the maliciousness of the disease had passed, and it passes in 3 or 4 days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And therefore they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, as soon as it was cured;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a young maiden take .i. knife and stab herself in the throat, slicing through some of the windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found that the blood had not come out through the throat or windpipe but instead was escaping through the wound itself.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried and sewed up the wound, healing her as best I could;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and had not the maid been bled, and returned after to her natural state;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that in cutting the epiglottis one should have no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This hernia is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large abscess in the color of ash, and it occurs mostly in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it is according to two ways: natural and accidental; where nature has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accident happens in two ways, one of which is similar to a boil that comes out of our veins, and the other way is like an abscess that comes from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and one should not operate with force unless in the smallest part, and test and examine throughout the entire opening:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it like a boil, and cannot push through at all, then cut it as one cuts a boil, and treat it throughout its entire depth, if there is nothing inside;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and surround it well, and treat it as it should be, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of doing this, all of which I will describe in detail.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and now I must explain the difference between a dislocation and an issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that discharge is hot and feverish, as long as the boil has not passed, and the pus is completed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the nose, there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains a sinus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a pimple, and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they are according to their appearances, either greasy or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of the nose, you should first test and examine it with an instrument called an "introducer", according to what its shape comes from in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses in the brain is to press on the dampest spot you find in the abscess, and gradually turn your fingers this way and that, until you feel the instrument has penetrated the core, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then withdraw the trocar, and be careful in case it jumps out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the flowing pus is clear, whatever color it has, treat it as I have described for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the trocar no pus comes out, know that it is dense, so treat it in the shape of a cross, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape off the crust on each side and guard the wound where it lies so you draw it clean with the needle;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out healthy, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will return to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if some remains and the pain troubles you, then employ corrosive powders on the wound, and constrict the wound, and apply hot ointments for abscesses, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, then cut the .10. lips of the wound, and treat it with that which causes pus.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein pulsating is contrary or other, you hurry and apply powdered vitriol to the spot, and leave it for 2 days or 3, until the wound suppurates, and the blood flow subsides; then return to cover what has remained of the night.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of the probing instruments, which come in 3 varieties: large, medium and small; and there are 3 squares, which are called 'albaret', and 1 that is called 'breb', and there are of 3 kinds: large, medium and small, for surrounding abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and are also like the needles used to sew sorcerers' charms, and are made of brass, iron or silver, and those that are yellow are best, and are more proven with black pitch for surrounding the channels of fistula;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and there are 3 kinds: large, medium and small, depending on the size of the opening of the fistula.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of warts are very varied, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and there are warts that have two curves in three ways as well.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and some warts that have three curves and are in three places as well; and some warts that have two curves, and are only in one place, but in three ways; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The main ones that are cut are sharp, and there are some that only cut on one side, so that the vein or nerve is not cut;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and these intrusions are placed in wounds, so that the patient does not perceive it when opening abscesses;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they are of three kinds: great, small, and medium, as you can see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and we do not use them except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar places.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling the shape of a pair of forceps, according to this form, with which blood is stanched:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed in the place that heals by filling the veins and arteries, and sometimes they are filled according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	At times the breasts of some men swell when they become corrupt, so that they look like women's breasts.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen; and if anyone wants to cure them, they should treat them according to the form given in this chapter from line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat and clean the wound with a cauterizing agent, then bring together the two lips of the wound with stitches and let it heal;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast shrinks and becomes soft due to its size, as it does in women, then cut it in two similar slits;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one holds the other at their end, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line [b] up to the line [g].
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about sewing and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely done, because the patient will not rest, or due to bleeding, then you should fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it remain until it dissolves the remnants and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are like hard scrofula and they have nodules, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b. to the line g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the content of the abscess is drained, then fill the wound with clean cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton and dress it with suitable ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are like scrofula, then treat them as we have said for fissures of scrofula, and if the wound is closed, then administer cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sewn shut, then abscesses often form, and likewise the vein swells and becomes abscessed.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if one knows this is due to the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your fingers, you will feel a dislocation; and when it is in the vein, there is a visible swelling;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is folly to cover this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits and on the arms and neck, and in many other places; it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, one should avoid the use of iron, and that which is at the head, one should also avoid, and in that which is inflammation of an artery, they should cut through the skin from above.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then perform the incision with a scalpel, and carefully cut the artery from the threads, so that it is exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then put a needle underneath it, and pierce it all the way to the other side, and constrict the artery with a double thread in .ii. places, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the .ii. arteries which are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then pierce the place between the .ii. threads of an instrument so that the pus comes out and the abscess is relieved;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then apply the treatment that causes bleeding, until the thread comes undone;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to the size of the vein, then you must hold in your hand as much of the pus from the abscess to the skin,
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle under the area you are holding in your hand and pierce it, and use a double thread so that you can pull it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then ligate the abscess, as I told you, on one of its two sides with the thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the thread will hold, insert another needle through the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and pull the threads tight in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then lance the abscess until the pus issues forth, then lance the superficiality of the chest and leave what is attached.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place on it a moist bandage soaked in wine and oil, then administer poultices and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, as abscesses come in the artery and vein, they also come in the nerves when they are injured, or from too great exertion, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens most often in the shoulders and in the hips, and everywhere there are joints, and it is a deep abscess, and its colour resembles the colour of the body, and in many places it has no pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is pressed firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not in the surface of the body but deep inside.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And it is silent in all parts, and does not go forward or backward, down or up, and for those who are in joints, one should not use a hot iron, lest there be contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And for those who are on the head or forehead, they should apply the spatumile to the skin.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with tongs and cut it at its base;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, they suspend it with a hook, then cut it open and remove the bone, and sew up the wound to heal it.
des grosses boces pendans	of large, hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes it happens in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" due to its resemblance to oats, and it has a subtle root and the scabs are thick. There are small ones and very large ones;
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw a man who had two in his belly which looked more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had thin roots, and were split open, and moisture was flowing out of them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I examined them and found one weighing 18 ounces and the other 6 ounces; and the treatment for this is to look if the swelling is moist, and if the color of the joint is white and moist with a thin root,
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if the wound is large and deep, and if the blood flows freely, then hurry to use the cautery. For often in deep wounds there are great flowings of blood, and if it flows away, then quickly use the cautery;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient terrified and fearful of the cut with the knife, then take a well-made thread and tie off the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then restrain it, and do not cease to twist the thread of the finger until it dislocates the joint, and piece by piece without effort; and if the roots are large, then have fear in dislocating it for the belly, but you can certainly dislocate half.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and be careful not to dislocate the testicle which is of a dusky color and poor sensation and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is a deep abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers next.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil has burst
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of a hernia comes from cauterization of a wound or a fissure in the syphilis, and it is on the belly and some of the bowels, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from flatulence;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is from the rupture of syphilis and from the exit of the bowels, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a slight thing without pain, and it opens from various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with their fingers, it pops out, and then returns in, and sometimes it is dried up, and increases a lot at the entrance of the bath and through hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is from moisture, it is a slight thing, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, it does not constrict at all; and if it is from blood, it opens through these signs of large and hard abscesses, and is fixed according to a certain quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to windiness, then there is swelling in the area, and the treatment is to look at whether the appearance is caused by blood from an artery or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	If it is necessary to let the wound heal. For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or bowel, then you must instruct the patient to hold his breath and be completely still, then sign all around the belly;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to lie down quickly between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the area you have marked for the entire spasm.
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then cut through the top half of the abscess to the large nail;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it tightly with a strong thread or a strong silk string, and let the patient fasten it himself;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then open the top half of the extended abscess over the string, and push your finger in, and feel for the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it stuck to the intestine, loosen it and push the intestine back inside the abdomen.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the gallbladder, take it at its base and cut away the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein causes resistance, then go around it carefully and return to your work. Take two needles, thread them with strong thread, and insert the needles where you made the cross-shaped incision.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then, pull the abscess in four directions using the needles, and if you can, remove the needles and let the area drain until it is clean. Scrape away any dead flesh.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or cut it when it is small and tender, then treat the wound as needed, and lance the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the wound as needed and bind it up.
dou chancre	for sores
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the types of sores and how to treat them with medicine, including cauterization with iron; now we shall speak of sores appearing in the throat, and great care is needed in their treatment. Ancient scholars say that when sores appear in places where they can be reached by scraping, such as on the nipples, thighs, or other similar areas, they should be completely removed at their onset. However, once they become large and chronic, one should not attempt to treat them, for I have never seen anyone healed from such sores, nor has anyone ever been healed from them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when it is in place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you sometimes purge the patient of black bile; then make him bleed if he has manifest fullness; then prepare the site for the operation; then shave the area around the ulcer and the head of the wound, and the bone all around without leaving anything; and let the blood run out completely, and squeeze well the site with your hand or something, and if the bleeding from the incision of the artery or vein makes you feel uncomfortable, cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then treat the wound with other treatments until it heals.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have already discussed the appearances of dropsy and how the accumulation of fluid is caused, as well as the signs of each type of dropsy, and the treatment through medicine and surgery. Now we will focus on the latter; you should not use surgery for two types of dropsy: tympany and hydroperitoneum, as these are very dangerous conditions. So, if you are treating a patient with dropsy that is called "eclites," and medication does not help, then consider whether the patient is weak or has other ailments besides dropsy, such as digestive issues and similar conditions; in such cases, do not use surgery, as there is a risk of complications. However, if the patient is strong and their only issue is dropsy, and they are neither too young nor too old, then you may proceed with the following surgical treatment:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Take the patient by the right hand and press his belly to force out the urine into the lowest part of the penis. Then take a spatulum according to this form: It should be pointed at both ends, but not so narrow that it can enter all the way to the intestines when inserted, nor so wide that it can cause bleeding.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then examine if the hydropsy is in the intestines: You should split beneath the navel on the right side three fingers' width deep. If it's due to liver disease, then the split should be on the left side three fingers' width deep; and if it's due to the spleen, then on the right, and the patient must not lie on the split so that the excess fluids do not flow into that weak area.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce all the way through to the instrument, and stop up the urethra, and pull your hand away from the spatulum in between the skin and the glans, as if skinning to the thickness of a fingernail or nail; then pierce the glans until the spatulum reaches the desired depth, and that is the location of the hydropsy. Then pull it out and stop up this instrument which is like a small silver needle, made of brass or light bronze, with a small hole on the underside; three holes on one side, two on the other, and one on the opposite side; the tip is shaped like a feather, and that is the form of the incision from which scribes cut feathers.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	at the head of this instrument is the alemele, so that when the instruments come to water, they now descend upon the instrument; empty therefore half or one third part, for if you empty more than is fitting in that hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit through the weapon, or he will faint away, or he will approach death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the malady indicate, and his pulses; then withdraw the instrument and retain the water, which is now retained by the heart that blocks the orifice that is above the syphus, of which I have spoken, which you pierce in this manner; then renew the instrument on the following day if you see the patient suffering from this, and draw off a small quantity of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	do this on one day, and beware of following it up until there remains but a little water. And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave in much water, then use the cure of sepulture or hot sand, and with much sweating in a bath and in the sun, and drink no wine; and the cure of medicines that are drying, as far as he is healed, and cauterize upon the stomach and upon the liver and upon the spleen after the drawing off of the water, just as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.
