Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is important for the midwife to know the natural signs of childbirth, and to understand what to look for when you see a woman struggling to breathe and desiring to smell aromatics; then you know that the baby is about to be born quickly. The natural birth occurs when the baby emerges head-first, with the placenta following close behind; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly so that the baby is delivered swiftly. For when the baby descends, the placenta follows, and the mother's body is cleansed of its excess fluids through a good purification ritual; anything else is not considered natural. Sometimes, however, the baby may present feet-first, or may emerge from the torso, arms, or abdomen, and in rare cases, the birth may be inverted, with the baby's head facing upwards instead of down. In such cases, it is crucial for the midwife to be wise and knowledgeable about these variations, guard against mistakes and disappointments, and I will now describe all the different positions and how to assist in each case.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the baby is born head-first in a natural delivery, and the woman is struggling, and her vitality is weak, then have her sit on a stool or be supported by other women; prepare an aromatic oil made from cooked celery seed or fenugreek, and then use a small spatula to apply it between her buttocks, as follows:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and split the placenta, and press her nails into her skin until the fluids inside flow out; and press her belly so that the baby descends, and if he doesn't descend, then give the woman a enema with a mixture of fenugreek and olive oil; then have her sneeze and cough to stimulate her bowels, and hold her mouth and nose closed for an hour: then the baby will be delivered.And if both hands emerge, then gently push them back in one by one; but if they cannot go back in, then have the woman sit on a chair, and lift her feet up so that they are elevated; then tilt the chair backwards so that she is lying down, and if the hands still won't go in, and the baby is dead, then grasp the hands at the knuckles and pull them out, and deliver the baby in the same way.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	of the child's feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes out of its feet, it should be pushed upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it slowly and gently until it is even;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then grasp the foot and extend it gently.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When it jumps up to the armpit, instruct it to grab, and make it sneeze with this condition;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps out, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump out as we have said, then pull it back and forth gently until it is in its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be easy.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come out as we have said, take mussel shell, and oil of sesame, and molten gum, and grind all in a mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and apply this ointment to the woman's privates and drive it out.
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	Then have her sit in warm water up to her ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	And when she is soft underneath, make a collar of myrrh and put it on her, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then have her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and pinch her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for the child will come out soon.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the birth of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this way, then he puts his hands little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then let him be supported on his neck, and let his feet hang down, and let him lie on a bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and bends his hands little by little, then presses his hands on the belly, and lifts the cushions underneath, until she is ready to pass down;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the fetus does not emerge, then take her feet and move them about, then move her belly upwards, then push with your hands;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and deliver the child little by little; and instruct the woman to press herself until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the child's exit, which comes out as wide as a hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	I must find a way to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if they cannot bring it back, then have the woman stand up and walk.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If she cannot walk, then let her lie on a bed and raise her legs straight;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the medicine that I have described;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	if she does not give birth, then have her sit on a chair, then study how to bring the hand back;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and turn the baby according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and tell her to squeeze until the baby comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the baby's exit on its neck, and have her hands spread out, and her face turned towards her mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	I must tie her hand, then turn it little by little, and hold it gently;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, then place on it a poultice of alum and oil as we have said, then instruct that it move little by little.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, then let her sit on a chair, and instruct her to hold it in; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way for all of the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes out in this way for all of the afterbirth, then catch the afterbirth with your fingers, as long as the moisture is expelled;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child bites on its face and neck, and the mother slaps it, let it not be restrained, and the child will die.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, as far as it should go, and instruct the woman to hold herself back at times:
adonques si istra legierement.	then if it is too loose.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Twins are a strange thing, and do not live long if they are born prematurely.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiplied and separated by the placenta which divides them, which is attached to the womb;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they issue just as naturally as a single child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they bleed a lot, then treat as we have said, and be subtle in your movements, and quickly and lightly do what she does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and act thus as it benefits their health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes they are formed in the womb as one or two or three or four or five or six or seven or more, up to fifteen, and they are all shaped like children according to the measurement of the glorious sage,
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is fitting that the surgeon know all this, for by chance a similar thing might happen to him;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	then act according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you are treating a woman for a dead child or fetus, as I have said in the division, and no blood comes out, and you are compelled to use manual pressure;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	if you need to know whether the woman is of sound health and has no fear of death.
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	the woman should be lying on her back with her head tilted down and legs lifted up.
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the midwife should use a ten-part mixture to apply to her womb, if she is lying in bed, so that the child can be delivered.
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	Then rub the mouth of the mother with moist oils, mixed with musk, altée, and fenugreek, and linseed; then anoint the midwife's hands with these oils and musks.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then press them gently into the wound, then bind it up in the usual way where it is convenient,
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and be careful that the child does not slide down onto its head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if it thrusts them into itself in its eyes or throat or mouth or under the beard or near the armpits,
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the dislocation is in the feet, strike or press at the middle of the shins;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he holds the needle in his right hand and places the thread between the fingers of his left hand, and ties it around all of his fingers lightly, and inserts the needle into any of the holes we have described so that it reaches the hollow place.
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is how the needle should be formed:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then pierce with another needle, or a third one if you need it, so that the extraction is even.
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then they are moved evenly back and forth to extract it, and the needles should be bitten down upon to hold them in place, as shown in this image:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if a part remains, then anoint the ball of one of his fingers with oil, and press it into that part, and draw out the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if nothing remains, then place this joint or a higher one, and do this until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot bring it back due to the dislocation,
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	then you must wrap it in .a. cloth, so that it all comes out.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then press on the joint of the sole or on the ankle; and so you should do with the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the head of the child is large and it is narrow in the outlet, or it has a sharp point
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	you should push the spathomile between your fingers, pierce the head, and draw out the water
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you can use the instrument called "almidach", of which the shape comes with the instruments in this chapter;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and so, the infant is naturally born with a large head;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then pull out the bones with tongs,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the head pops out and is forced, it is split until the moisture that is in the wound comes out;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if she cannot come out, then cut her into pieces as much as you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or beneath the ribs, then you must pierce it so that the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is above his feet, the pulse is light, and the breath comes easily to the mouth.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is swollen in the belly or the groin, then you must strap it tightly with a bandage around the hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and pierce the belly or the groin, so that the moisture which is within flows out;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if the other limbs are paralyzed, and the eyes remain
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	then he bathes his hand in warm water, and leads it up to the mouth of the wound;
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	then he adds one ounce or two ounces, and draws it out;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has formed there, one should not work on it,
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	then you must apply moist and greasy things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and he applies poultices, and softens and moistens with water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the fetus is on its side, and you can make it even, then administer what we have said about a living child:
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one has no strength, then cut it into pieces, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, if they are given what we have said for abscesses that come in the sea;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and bloodletting comes, it should be placed in restraining water, and other remedies are administered.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose fetus had died within her; then another was sewn over him, and the other died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time an abscess came in his arm, and swelled so much that it opened, and began to discharge profusely.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the priest, and I thought long and hard, but could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong drawing plaster, and out came a bone, and after a few days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	Examine the wound, and with your hands pull out bones until the woman feels better.
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	And let the woman walk like this for a long time, and she will suddenly feel a bit of relief from her pain.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I have only included this chapter because when masters find an unusual case, they should know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the dislocated shoulder to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the press, to which one adds the books; and at .2 turns as .2 heads of .2 lines.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nevertheless, let the horns be more slender in the constrictor, and made of boxwood or of ivory;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the beam be one digit wide, and the edges of the trees one digit, and long a palm and a half;
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and in the two beams there are two adjustments of this same wood, which are firmly joined together, one half a palm long or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two settings are placed in the mouth of the wound to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of pincers;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and it has two heads with two settings, as you can see, a palm long and two fingers wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see the wound opened with all the instrument, let the woman sit on a bed, hanging her feet and opening her legs,
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then insert the two pieces of the instrument into the wound, and hold the head of the instrument under between your thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand on the whole instrument, just as you did with the tongs equally, according to the amount that you see the opening of the wound, until the patient makes the face she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all decorated, and their appearances are multiplied; and when the patient sees them prepared, the action is faster and higher in people because of their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair over the instrument, but prepare it, for their need is inexcusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the placenta is retained after childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath and then make her sneeze with a scent, and pinch her nose and mouth tightly.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	And if she vomits, all the better.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, take a pitcher and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the mother, such as calendula, rue, anise, chamomile, and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water over the fire; then put one end into the pitcher and the other into the mouth of the mother,
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and the dye as long as the vapors come within the wound; then make it sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the pus comes out quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment and is not gone, then command the patient to wet her left hand in oil of wormwood or in a poultice of alder, and then put it into the wound.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and wants to find the pus; and when she has found it, she should squeeze and stretch it gently little by little, so that the wound does not hurt with the extraction;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but it must be moved slightly to the right and left, and then pulled; so it will come out and release itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the wound is narrow, we have described the treatment of sneezing, and of the fume of herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not [healed] by all that we have said, then beware that you do not cut;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that the person at the mouth of the wound ties it to the woman's thigh, then cleanse with four-fold ointment;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	if it can be released and reset, then it will come out; but still, when it is released in this way, there comes a bad odor to the stomach and head, and it harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If necessary, suitable fumigations should be used for this: some ancient writers have tried fumigation with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The instrument used to fumigate the woman for retained placenta and afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it should be made of glass like a cane, with a slender neck and wide base to sit over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let there be fume over the coals, and the dye until it is wasted, and start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born without their fundaments pierced; instead, they have a thin membrane.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	So the midwife should pierce that membrane with her finger, and not with a spike or needle; and she should be careful not to tear it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on wet linen with wine and oil, then dress it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will heal, then put a wooden splint through the wound and leave it for several days, then remove it when the child wants to walk around.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes the healing comes suddenly from a wound or an abscess; then it must be covered suddenly: then it should be treated, as we have said, with a wooden splint.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulæ which come underneath the fundament are nodular, and growing in size, or from within the fundament, or in the space of two parts.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if there is one or more fistulæ; and when this nodulation is old, it opens, and then moisture causes a white discharge or thin pus.si l’on queré qu’elle soit seure et close, si convient que li médecins la fasse boire vin clere ou eix,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulæ are piercing; and they are caused by what comes out in egestions or emissions when the patient makes an egestion, and sometimes a worm will jump out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulæ which penetrate as far as the bladder, and halfway down the penis; and they can reach the joint of the thigh, and down to the testicles.Et si a fistules qu’advenent desoz le fondement et par les costes ou par la nuque, ou par le petis de la cuixe; et sont mals aincis.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one recognizes the fissure which seeps at the anus, and does not seep:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and you should stab your index finger or thumb into the anus, and stab a thin needle made of bronze or iron into the fissure when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is twisting, then you should stab a thin tent made of lead, or a horsehair, as far as you can feel the tent or hair with your finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you cannot feel it, and there is no egesta or flatulence or discharge as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	you know it does not pierce; then you hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula penetrates as far as the bladder or the duct of urine, and urine escapes, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced as far as the hip joint, then the vein bleeds as far as the spot.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the pain is not relieved, then it will be cured by boiling water and not by ointment.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and for these persian ulcers there is no cure other than work, and the folly of those who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	For that which is not Persian and not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have proven.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	And let the patient lie on his back, and lift his legs up to his thighs, and have his thighs inclined towards his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then insert a tent of iron, or of lead if there is tortuosity, as far as you know the tent goes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the pain is felt around the anus, you must insert your index finger.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and if you feel that the membrane has been pierced; and if it is uncovered where you feel between your finger and the flesh, then know that it has been perforated;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if you do not work on it, it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One says that some can be healed, but it rarely happens;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help which one does, then one scorches the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and stuff it all hot into the fistula as far as the anus; and do this twice or thrice, as long as you know that these charred tissues are burned, which look like a feather of a bird.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	And then cure it with moist bandages in butter, as long as the char comes out, and then cure with ointment that softens and heals.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If he is thus healed, it is good. If not, it cannot be healed otherwise.
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent enters and does not penetrate to the right which is in the foundation, and there is between your finger and the tent a thick covering of flesh or skin, and you see the fistula below the covering of the heart;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	cut at the beginning of the fistula, and then stop it before the tent, and then cauterize afterward, as far as the head of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the tent will be delivered and will fall out; then cut away the false flesh that looks like a bird's feather, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pus comes out and flows between you and the wound, then cauterize it with fire or with an astringent medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For fire cautery brings together two things: the burning of the flesh and the clotting of blood and the drying of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	Then treat with tented bandages moistened in butter or ground substance, until the site drips fluid and the flesh burns through to the bone.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then treat the wound with sudatory poultices of hard, dry matter.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way to the bottom of the foundation, and is removed from the body, put your finger or foundation in it, and inquire about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tent, and between them is the thread or the cloth, or it is about to pierce, there is no strength except through faith and hope, by administering one of the three remedies:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can, put in tents and cure it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	And do not go too deep, so that you do not cut the tenant who holds the foundation, and let the evacuations come out through there as they wish.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance if it is cured, or you remove that covering and clean it after it has been cut away from the foundation, or by tent or other pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then mend that broken bone which is in the wound, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then endeavor to heal the wound and to keep the fistula in the part above the foundation: if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes they are fistulas according to this manner: and it is when you insert the tent into the fistula, and it is on the side of the foundation below the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	Take a tent pierced at the tip in this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he inserts a twisted thread into it, and he inserts the tent along the entire thread into the fistula until it reaches the tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it pierces through the margin inside, then pull out the thread from that opening, just as you would push your finger into the fistula.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and draw the head with thread, and bring the two heads together, and hold them tightly for one or two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it sometimes, until the threads cut through the flesh between the two;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then heal the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open on its own, then you must make it open in every way that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to cover the wound with a bandage, then treat it, as we have said, until it has healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the spiny spatomile, which they make into a fistula, is very sharp and pointed on one side.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	And on the other side it is not, so that one should not cover it, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are of two types: sometimes they are inside the anus like grains of resin, and there are small ones and large ones, and some ooze blood.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	Some have one or more of these hemorrhoids outside the anus and at the top of the anus; but those that are outside have a little moisture,
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and ooze water or a little yellow water or a little blood, and are the same color as the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those who have them inside the anus is that you command the patient to stay in bed until the anus heals and the hemorrhoids fall out.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	If you rush it and grab it with tweezers or your fingernail, then pluck it at its root.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	And if they cannot be held with tweezers due to moisture, then take them with a cloth or cotton or a piece of camel's hair.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	Then pull it out with your fingers, pluck it and powder some warm powdered cautery on top.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	Or you can cauterize them as described in the chapter on cauterization, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot come out, then cleanse the patient with a biting and harsh enema to wash what is in the foundation so that it can come out clearly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	if the patient presses himself, and the thread comes out from under the foundation, then the cure is easy;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and you should grab them with your fingernail or tweezers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until they are healed and the incision is no longer feared.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary to administer the stitch in this way: take a twisted thread and put it into a needle, then pull the thread from above and pierce the needle from the other side, and return both ends of the thread under the needle,
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is too wide; then tighten the thread tightly, tie off the thread, remove the needle, and do likewise with all the others, leaving one to drain the excess blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then place over the wound a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate, and then apply pressure on it, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then leave it until they heal, and when they are healed, then treat them with ointments and other treatments.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from dryness of the anus or rectum
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Drying of the bowels occurs often in the intestines, due to constipation from natural causes, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If necessary, cut into the skin at the tip of a spatula or your fingernail, so that it does not become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	Then dry it until it is hard and as it should be.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	And if it cannot harden, then restart the scraping more fiercely than before, until it heals completely and is scoured.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it until it heals.
dou fremit	where there is trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A freckle is a small discolouration on the skin, which goes deep under the skin and moves around a lot.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes the trembling affects the fingers, and one feels it like a deadness from the trembling, and it comes all over the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a cane of goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place this cane on the vein, until the purple circle surrounds the vein all around;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then return your hand to the entire cane as you press all around the vein, and put it in deeply, and squeeze the vein from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see fit, make a cane of bronze or iron according to this shape, and let it be thin underneath and drawn out on top:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	nor pierced, so that it may hold the finger, and press firmly. And if you see fit, cauterize the vein, just as it is described in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes they are made of silver or brass, or melted copper or wire; and sometimes they are made small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those which are administered for the treatment of children and the weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large enema is above wide, or the belly is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has an opening where the belly is tied, as you can see, and the anus is pierced inside; and it has two openings on one side, and one on the other;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the belly where one puts the medicine is made of a beast's bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes;
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and between each hole there is a distance of one digit, then insert into these holes a strong cord of twisted gut or thread wound around, and assemble the belly so that it looks like a goat;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong cord, then cleanse; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	Let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the clistere with oil or egg white, or similar thing, then insert it gently;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then the minister squeezes both ends of the clistere together until it is empty, then withdraw the clistere, and let the patient lie on his side,
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to come out, then hold it as long as he can, and if he sleeps for a night afterwards, it is even better.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use the clistere for the disease of stomach ache, and the medicine rushes to come out, then repeat it until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if hemorrhoids are in the anus or an abscess, then use an enema as thin as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	This is the form of the thin enema that the skin should be stretched onto:
des plaies	Of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the division the cure of wounds; now we will discuss the cures by hand and medicine according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and by what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The objects that cause wounds are from stone, and sword and knife, or lance or staff or arrow, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or according to the places in the body where they are made, such as a wound on the neck, or head, or thigh, or belly, or liver, and similar organs;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for the memory will come to him in his chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, one should take care whether it is from a stone or similar object, and the skin is still intact but the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt whether it is a hot abscess: then have the patient bleed from the head immediately if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the bleeding be in the opposite direction to the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and let the patient avoid excesses of wine and rich foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to bleed, then his diet should be reduced, and he should neither drink wine nor eat meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and apply a poultice to the wound, if a hot abscess comes, only wet cotton in rose oil, or in astringent wine;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it is still bleeding and not moved by the air, a powder that I will describe soon;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it has been moved by the heat, then put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a sword, and the lips cannot be brought together with tenting, then stitch them together, as I will describe for abdominal wounds.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and gapes, and holds only by a little, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard skin in place of the hide.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and instruct the patient to eat coarse meats such as testicles and cooked wheat, also like fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rot in the hide, and it isn't attached to the bone, then cut off the rot completely, and pour out the pus, then cure it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which isn't clotting, and cannot be staunched with medicine, then tie it off, and if you find it loose, bind it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is light; you should put on this powder which heals as soon as the burn is healed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part, dragon's blood two parts, quicklime three parts, and powdered very finely,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and employ the wound, and bind it tightly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and leave it untouched if it doesn't swell; for one removes the medicine only when it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with chalk alone, when one doesn't have incense or dragon's blood, but that the wound is moved by the fire.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the fire has moved the wound, one should stop it immediately and not put any of this powder on it;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digestive ointments, or barley flour made with water and honey, until the swelling goes down;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat other treatments until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of the bone comes with the wound, and it is small, I will extract it with subtle pincers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you below about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound on the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the neck and it is single, then there is no difference between it and one in the head, but if the nerve of the neck or artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's a nerve, there is nothing else that can be done but to leave the wound untreated and not put anything constricting on it, because it harms the nerves and causes them to withdraw.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuations are with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	But for the medicine underneath, use warm water, and mix it with rose oil, and cooked fennel also washed in warm water,
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other damp stones according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then cut and bind it, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep, and she has a fever and is swollen and full of pus, then pierce her or cut her lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and bleeding occurs, then ligature it, and cauterize it if necessary;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the food conduit is kept open, through which the food goes,
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	cut the windpipe above the base of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	then stretch it gently, and leave it for a few days, then treat it with purifying ointments until it heals;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has caused depression in the bone, then treat it thus;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, pull them out as far as you can, and those that you cannot reach, leave until the wound can heal.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and it should be cleaned and aligned at the site of dislocation;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, apply the powder I have described.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have said in that chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, then examine if there are no windings around the wound: you will therefore know that the wound is deadly;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep and the wound is fresh with all its blood, do not put the powder on it at the first hour or ligature it because of the blood that will ooze out profusely,
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and return to the body, and keep the patient warm;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put on an attractive ointment, and bind it .ii. times a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you don't have ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to draw out moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and let the patient sleep on the wound for .iii days, or .iv., or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if a spasm, or trembling of the body, or chills do not come;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good signs, then you know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat it with poultices and other remedies until it is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal, and there is a fistula, then you know that there is a wound; then treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is simple, or worse, on the front or back, then treat it as described above;
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, by stitching; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has torn bits, then probe the wound, and pull out the shards if they are loose;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not loose, then let the wound fester, so as to ease the extraction;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds in other members, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	from a rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from a large wound, sometimes the intestine, or the nerves of the intestines, by which the entrance of air;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the sewing is more difficult, and sometimes the smaller wound is worse than the larger,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because one puts them in again more easily, if one doesn't put them in hot and cold;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, they contract more with pins.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and for this reason it is useful to move the soft wound, and therefore one must move the intestines to their place more than others .ij.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that hernia of the abdomen occurs in .iiij. ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the .ij. common hernias occur in the abdominal wall,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitching of other wounds on the body, and two other special stitches are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	nevertheless they are more appropriate with stomach wounds, and I will name and explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and something from the intestines protrudes out,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and it can be treated by one of two methods:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or from the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in such a way:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	wet a sponge or soft cloth in lukewarm water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you boil in water squinant and cypress and spice,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and boil the intestines until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes it makes restraining wine, and the soul is moved away to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling go down, then open the intestines with water or old wine are cooked,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	For by this means the entrance is contracted to a small space.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, they make a small cut in the instrument with which they cut hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first cure is bloodletting rather than cutting,
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	which one should not do without great need;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument to split it with:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if cut within the curve and not out, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines jump out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if he puts it back according to its natural shape in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you can, because this is useful.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large and it is in the lower part of the abdomen,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	you should make the patient lie on his back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the part below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then put the head and the foot higher than the parts below.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the .ij. parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	then put the affected part higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and so you should treat those wounds which are large and small.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, apply what you have prepared,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then have at hand a minister of pity who will spread ointment over the entire wound with his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the edges of the wound,
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common method of sewing.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	Take a needle or several needles depending on the size of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave a distance of half a digit from the edge of the wound, and insert a needle with a strong thread through it;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce both sides of the skin with both sides of the edge,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the skin inside, as long as you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and put together the two heads of the sutures;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then pierce it with a double thread through the needle in two places,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then bring together the two heads of the wound smoothly,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then leave .i. space, and I put another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this according to how many needles you need,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the entire wound is bound up;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	let the needles be medium-sized, between fine and thick,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because fine needles pierce all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot pierce well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore they should be medium-sized;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and one must not push the needles too deep into the flesh and through the skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	that they do not cut and open the wound before it is healed.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut the tips of the needles so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and put tents or bandages on the needle heads to keep them in place,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of sewing with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because one or two needles are enough.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is where you bring together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the wound with one needle and a strong thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have cut through all four of these bones together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then reset the needle in the part where you began, in the manner that one sews clothes;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a distance between each stitch equal to the thickness of a thumb;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitching should be done on a man,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed up a wound that a man had on his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which he had received from a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm in length,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and the intestines were protruding more than two palms in length,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was below his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought him back the intestines after they had been out for 24 hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was sewed up until the 15th day, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they had judged him that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat it with ointment, because I was in a place where there were neither any of these things nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put cotton wool on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and pierce it from the outside just to the inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the right heart directly, then lay the end of the siphon or tube on top of where you have inserted the needle
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce another part of the inside up to the outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the technique for this suturing is that you sew just like a leatherworker sews hides,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and leave the siphon once on one side and then pull it through to the other, so that the suturing is all completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of sewing, which Galen describes properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	if it is like how one joins two pieces of wood together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and applies the end of one piece to the other end, in such a way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	push a needle or awl through both pieces near their ends, and only pierce those spots,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two shoulders of the syphyllis;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and pierce it from the outside inwards just to the inside,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as two shoulders of the syphyllis;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce one and the other from the outside inwards just to the inside, in two other shoulders of the syphyllis that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the better way of sewing and the more common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galen says these words, and some testify to them,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one must sew the belly with .ii. needles, having thread in each;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corroded holes;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is in the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	the sutures are more painful than others in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound full of blood, as long as the heat has not moved it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	If you reset it to allow the intestine to return, then put on the binding powder over the wound.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	And if it burns, put some ointment on it that is available until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And cut the thread and sew up the wound, and use myrrh and honey.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat the wound as with other wounds until it is healed.The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicine, put on old cotton immediately when it begins to ooze.
