et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you don't need any other medicine for various wounds when they are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound will affect the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	if necessary, you should moisten it with a little warm oil, or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it around the angles and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or swelling in the bowels, and this happens many times,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then treat him in the manner that I tell you. If he has dark, watery diarrhea, and especially if the swelling comes just up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierces inside, and you can tell when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine that is called "young" cannot heal when it is raw,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it is because of the thinness of the veins that they are, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the thread jumps out of the wound, it pulls it back as well as the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and turned white or black, then you must tie the area that has turned black so that blood does not flow into it,
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are veins and arteries in it;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligament,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two shoulders hanging from the part below the wound until it is released to ease the extraction when the splinters are removed, and the wound is healed.
de la routure dou boueil	of the route of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are ruptured, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	one can restore it in some cases,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw a man who was stabbed in the belly with a lance;he had a small wound and yet he survived.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and became a fistula, and from it issued flatulence and winds;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it with cautery according to what I could do, and did not cease subtilizing until it was healed and the wounds closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw that it was healing, I doubted that the patient had discomfort in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm done, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experiencers say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in such a way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take fine thread, then bring together the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the thread has opened the mouth, place it above the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	if it pulls out its mouth above;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then grabs its head, and it stays so that it cannot untie itself,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another tremor after in the same way, until the wound is completely healed;
et cout la plaie.	and watch the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If these parasites are found in the intestines and cause no harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	one can tie the intestine with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in such a way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this intestinal thread that is very thin,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the head of this thread a fine, twisted linen thread,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then pass the thread through the needle, and sew up the intestine, and relase it in the wound;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of sewing up the intestines is not useless except according to the path of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the great intestines, there is no healing without subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	You should know that any wound or abscess, when it erupts, is universally called a "fistula",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and especially when it is deep and narrow.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	A fistula is according to the definition a hard, white nodule without pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is as smooth as a bird's feather;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it is clear, and sometimes thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small, and sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the section on wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no scabs,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	these are caused by one of the eight causes;
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by a little wound or injury;
ou por sa malice;	or because of their wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh within, and on the lips, which does not let the flesh grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much bowing;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the skin is loose, and the tissue is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good for the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a form of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or by the property of the region is delayed digestion, and late health, and swollen by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I will tell you about the treatment for a fistula that is done with the hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistulas occur throughout the body's limbs;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from large veins and arteries and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the syrinx, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in some of the sides,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet;The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it affects the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this way are painful to heal, and there is no benefit but labor and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the point that I have described, and you are confident in the treatment,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you see it, take a tent of bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, so take it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is crooked, then search for a thin tent of lead,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because the lead bends with the crookedness.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	And if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot well search it out by tents,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then cleanse it through one of its openings,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for moisture quickly runs from one hole to another, and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then you shall let it bleed until you know whether there is bone or nerve involved, and it is deeply pierced;
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it most;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and once you truly know the location, whether it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places I have told you about, according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the dirt and rotten cart-wheels that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then clean the wound until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is quite deep in a straight line, you should cut it open as far as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I wet tents with medicine water, and insert them into the fistula up to its head,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine corrodes the surplus that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I apply healing ointments to the healthy flesh, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve afflicts the principal limbs as we have said,
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered and there is corruption and darkness, then treat it until all the corruption is removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then clean it with things that are soothing until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if he is not cured, and returns as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not gone to the source:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	uncover and dig as deep as you can,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is like this without pain, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other way, let it heal naturally;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone that has become corrupt, and you can pull it out with tweezers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if he extracts it with an instrument suitable for this purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, he should extract them all without leaving any behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture makes it difficult, and there is no mistake or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	then cut through flesh and moisture and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then place something upon the wound to promote suppuration,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it remain until pus has formed around the bone,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will have a looser joint;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you just treat the infection until all the darkness is gone,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large amount of corruption, and it comes to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it needs to be cut out and covered up completely until the corruption is reached, then clean the wound until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	I will tell you of a fistula which happened to a man in his leg;
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take example and aid from it in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about 30 years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that arose within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the matter came out of the leg, and it was swollen with a large abscess, and there was no pus to drain from it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but they looked at their folly so much that they opened the abscesses
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and many materials came out and became a fistula, and many openings came from which all pus and moisture flowed from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many looked for a cure for two years, and there was no wise person in the art of medicine,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as long as I was called there, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what runs through the pores of the body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the youth's body turned red and had a yellow hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I set up a tent at one of these openings, and then I examined all the openings,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that they came together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I therefore hurried, and pressed one of the orifices until I uncovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came up to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I removed what appeared to be rotten bone, and believed that there was no other corruption except for that which I removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to treat the wound with strong medicines for a long time, but it would not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then begin again, and expose the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found the corruption continued in the bone, and removed it, and then closed the wound;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not until I split the bone for a palm's width, and I drove it out to all its root,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medicine; and it was healed and closed quickly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and one must not repeat the operation except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and for fear of his death which I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For by the evacuation he often bled, but he was entirely healed,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and there grew in the place of the bone hard flesh, and he was of good disposition and did not have any harm or evil anywhere, nor in going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if a bone is broken anywhere in the body, it must be treated thus:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a thread, and tie it to the head of the bone which appears,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and have someone pull it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and take another thread of thicker wool than the first, and tie it to the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and are the head, so that you draw the corrupted flesh underneath,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the area where you see it is swelling, so that the swelling does not spread to the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a hot brand or a table under the bone to cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and one must draw as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and draw again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is broken and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then it discovers all the flesh; then put under it a brand
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then sear from one side of the corruption to the other, and make the blister as long as the corruption, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in a joint, cut open the joint and sear the bone on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the dislocation is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other remedy but to cover it;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the dislocation is at the base of the hand or the foot, it is a very serious matter,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nevertheless you must examine the patient, how it appears to them;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way you can, but be careful not to damage the veins or nerves;The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the chisel and the files for covering these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of the ears

dou feu	fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulders may protrude due to internal causes or external causes;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have treated that corrosion with remedies, and they do not help,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then you should cover the limb up to where the corrosion is,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes through death, or through the greater evil, from the defect of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the sign is that the limb becomes black, as if it were burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and then comes darkness, after which the corrosion of the limbs spreads from limb to limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and throughout the body; so you must hurry to cover it up,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is due to the sting of poisonous beasts, such as scorpions from the sea, vipers, and similar creatures,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is on the head or neck, then cover it, and do not give it any space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes to the hand, then grip at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, then grip near the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is deadly,
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no remedy for this except by reducing its power;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and so too when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then grip after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, cut off the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises to the leg, cut at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to kill the patient with a stab to the throat;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way of binding the member whether above or below, it should be tied above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and one minister stretches one of the strings downstream, and another minister stretches the other string upstream,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you loosen the rope that is between the two strings to a width of one palm, so that the bone is exposed;

Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if there is bleeding when you operate, then cauterize the wound liberally.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the wounded member with an appropriate bandage and treat it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to a certain man in a dream:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	a darkness resembling a burn from fire occurred to him
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and this corrosion first appeared on his toe of the foot, so that it spread all over the foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he covered his foot and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and a long time after, the corrosion returned to the toe of the hand, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put upon him things that rebound after cleansing of the body, but he could not stop the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to cup his hand, and I did not want to, for I had no hope of rebounding the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I doubted that if I cut his hand, that he would die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the strength of the man was weak; and he despaired altogether, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he healed his hand;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	I have told this story only to show that one should do this, if they need to.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy part, and remains so long that it causes great swelling;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	then they rupture and drain, and the flesh remains, just like vessels;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin above is as thin as a loose napkin,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not reach to the bone or nerve, and such a malady is called 'healthy',
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called 'fistula';
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it extends to the bone, then it is called 'fistula'.;
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure is to wrap the skin all around it, especially when it is thin, as one would a piece of cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not worry about its destruction.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you are worried that the skin will rot, and the corruption is not complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then the cure is thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Look to see if the breasts are large, and if the bowels within are of foul odor.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	therefore cleanse them with an Egyptian medicine which is made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take asafétida, oil, and quicklime, in equal parts, and mix and cook them in a vessel over fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take according to your need, and make it with water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and use it as an enema in the breast, and tighten the orifice;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine in for .ij hours, then remove it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this a number of times, until the breast is deflated and the pore is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes they are blisterized with water of ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you should take ashes of vine wood, and pour water over them,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then strain it and blister with it as much as you know the wound is clean;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot endure it, nor Egyptian medicine nor water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if he is enema with water and honey or with a little litarge ground.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you can use honey and honeyed wine for the enema; let the honey have the property of cleansing and washing away.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the body perspire.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	And when you have done this and are sure that the intestines are well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if they use a cautery on him which produces pus within
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and you prepare an ointment with diaphoretic herbs, and apply it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you may cauterize him with certain medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken in the section on ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of his anus is small, and the tip of the cautery instrument cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if you enlarge it with an iron a little, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, then cut it and leave only enough room for the catheter to enter,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the orifice that urinates is above, then the cup or lower down where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bow is perfect, one does not allow the arrow to become lodged inside.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	set up the bow in such a way that it points to the lowest place it can reach,
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the bow is perfect, one does not allow the arrow to become lodged inside.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	prepare in such a way: that the bowstring runs smoothly down, and do not leave anything of the bowstring;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidating medicines to put over the breast,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and they are on a linen cloth that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then press with force the opening of the breast . The hole must be larger than the first .
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	Then there is a soft ointment on another piece of cloth according to the quantity of the opening,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it on the breast opening to align the bowels, and do not remove the large bandage for several days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	And the one who is on the breast opening, remove often to remove the bowels,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what flows from the bowels, whether it is poison or little or enough, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and be wary if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has spread in such a way, and you see the nature that jumps out of the opening of the breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the breast is open, and approaches the saint;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then loosen it in the morning, or midday, and when you loosen the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast milk flows in an unripe state after several days, know that the breast will not produce milk.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons flow after a long time, do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	because the saints are near. For there are people whose wounds fester for a long time, and those who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if milk does not flow from the breast after many days, know that the breasts will not open;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breasts are delayed in opening, and are distant, then apply medicines that are moist in substance but dry in virtue,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as with diaphoretics, for there is a great part of vitriol in them, and that is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take a definite ointment, and make it with rose oil, and mix in equal amounts of old wine;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and with the same mixture, thicken honey.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when a definite ointment is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them into powder over the honey while it is on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then they glue a piece of cloth, and press it onto the breast, and sometimes they administer an aromatic poultice,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of celestial lily, which is like wheat flour and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in the use of simple or compound medicines: grind them to a powder and place it on the honey I mentioned earlier and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	And if the wound is long and not healed by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then you know that the corruption is complete, and it makes an impression on the bone, or in the hard body, or in the soft tissue.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is an abscess that arises underneath the fingernail of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Or by a stone, or perhaps it sprouts in other parts;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it becomes diseased, and no attention is paid, then an abscess forms and bursts;
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they run and ooze pus until they reach the root of the nail, and sometimes they even cut all the way through;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corrosion reaches the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the shoulder is swollen and the colour is yellow.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat him as we have said in the previous section, and the treatment does not help,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	you must cut away all the excess that has accumulated under the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cautery is a great help if the bone and nail are healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses on the flesh, and begins to push out, and bleeds,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	you should place a thread under the nail so that it stops pushing against the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and draw it up gently and gently cut the flesh underneath,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and place burning and corrosive medications on top to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the swelling until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then dig it out and cut it away, because as long as the bone remains corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the tooth decayed, pull it out in the manner previously described,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the swelling until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wild, and biting, and it feels great pain, then you must treat it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then clip the fingernail of the big toe with a diagonal cut from above,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the cutting does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, put something on it to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a deaf person's hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	There are two types of warts that grow on people's hands by chance: they can be all fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes there is bone in them and sometimes nails,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some grow at the base of the joints, where the growth comes from the knuckles.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	He who is born with a hernia of the navel should not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and he who is born at the junction of the navel, by chance moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of the one who is fleshy is light, in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that grow at the root of the joint are difficult to cure; you must cover them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	For those growing on the back of the neck, you must first shave the hair around it in a circle up to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, cut the skin down to the bone with a suitable blade, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Joints can be united by birth, or by the joining of a wound, or by a burn, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is fitting that you correct this wound, so that its parts are restored according to their natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two tents or moistened cloths in rose oil, so that they do not adhere.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you place between two pieces of thin plywood, until the wound is closed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If adhesion occurs to one of his hands with the palm, correct that adhesion as it should be.
Des vils	Of the wicked
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large enveloped vessels filled with melancholy humours that come into various parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it happens more in legs of those who walk and labor and carry things, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him some purgative medicine, and then the basil drink.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with fire can be done in two ways: one is to use a cautery on the head of the wound, drawing out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is that you open the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The incision is done in this way: first, heat the leg with very hot water until the large vessels are made subtle,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then stretch the leg from the sick person from above the thigh to just below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then open the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide cut,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then squeeze and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient can tolerate;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bandage it, and instruct him to drink possets with black wine;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and start the evacuation and bleeding again when the veins are full, which benefits the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The treatment of it is as follows: shave the leg of the patient, if there is much hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put him in a bath and raise the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat it with fire, and then rub the area around the vein from the top of the knee to the foot, or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the vein, and blister it from each side, until it is sore when touched;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it appears red and black, and when it enters the skin, it looks like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then pierce it under the skin, so that it is raised up from the skin, and then it can be easily pulled out at the tip,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut into it in another place above it, twice; then scorch the skin over the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it up with a pair of tongs, as you have done before, and pull it out with another pair of tongs, as you did before;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another strip, or several if you need them, then lift it, and press it against the bottom of the foot,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull and lift it until you reach the second strip; then pull it out, strip by strip, until it is all removed, then press it down;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot pull and lift it, then thread a needle with strong, doubled thread,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	then tie it and pull it out, and insert the needle under a nail, and turn your hand back and forth until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and make sure it does not break, for if it breaks, then one cannot milk or raise it, and this brings harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have milked it entirely, then place on the site of the wound wool moistened with wine and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	you must split it twistingly, but do not break it; and milk it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one opens the vein is curved, and does not cut, so that it opens the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	It is of a large curve, because if it were thin, it would cut the vein; but it should be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in hot places where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and sometimes it grows elsewhere, and this happens from the scabs that form under the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	like serpents and worms that nestle between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this illness are that there is a great swelling in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then change the location, and the illness will begin to emerge, just as a plant's root emerges from the ground.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head is exposed, it is necessary to wrap a piece of woolen cloth around it, one and a half yards long, and tie it tightly.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	Let the woolen cloth hang down from the head to the leg, and every time he tries to get away, wrap him up in the cloth again, and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	If the cloth is too long, cut off a piece and wrap the rest around him, but do not cover his head at all while it is still coming out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	Because if you cover him completely, it will go back into the body and cause an abscess and swelling in that place, and a serious illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	it must be treated slowly and gradually until it reaches the head, and nothing should remain in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And sometimes this vein, when it is opened for five or ten inches, or even more,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and once a man came to me whose vein was opened for ten inches, and when you cover it, it makes one hole or aperture, and pierces all the way through,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that all fluids inside are discharged; and then administer warming medications for several days, then treat it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein opens on its own, especially when it breaks out at the joint of the foot, or in the foot,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there is a great gushing of blood; treat it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms which grow between skin and flesh:
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called "cattle disease" in our land, because it often happens to oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and there is a small worm that hatches between skin and flesh, and moves throughout the body going up and down,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it can be felt moving from limb to limb, until it breaks through the skin where it goes, and jumps out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by the putrefaction of certain humors, like worms and snakes and roundworms and tapeworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and it is feared for its maliciousness, for when it moves through the body, and it rises to the head, and comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance re-enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him being healed and milked, he cannot be restrained except when he wants to:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	So you must tie the area above and below with a strong, tight string,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then milk on top of it and if the venom is deep in his body and you do not draw it out,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you cauterize it with fire above, as it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye, then firmly pull the lash out from under the eyelid, and pull upwards.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	It is necessary to use a purifying medicine for the body to dissolve the bad humour that has been poured out,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and from eating putrid meats.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vomiting" in our language, and it is a pain that occurs in some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after, I saw it rise up like a worm at the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	quicker than anything else, as bright as silver when it moves from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain left that place and settled in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later it ran through the whole body until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then he told me that it turned around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how it moved from limb to limb like that, because I had never seen this disease progress in that way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had seen many who experienced pain moving from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I have not seen this happen to a woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because women's bodies are dry and their veins exposed,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason the wind is confined to a small space;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate and have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	examine it above and below thoroughly, then press upon it until that forced windiness leaves its place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it yourself,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the cure is done by someone who expels windiness, as with foul-smelling pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the part of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	Their diversity lies in that there are those with large points, and small, and barbed, and smooth.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those that have two angles, and of those that have teeth, and of those where there are parts;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and it breaks in any limb in two ways: either in a principal limb it breaks,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it therefore breaks in any of these limbs, and the signs of death that I will tell you about below appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must take care when extracting this arrow, because death comes after in many cases.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if the wound is not completely healed and there are no bad signs, then pull out the arrow and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And when the sign of the brain is seen, the arrow has pierced the bone and passed through to the brain, and the pus that flows out from it,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is a cut and bleeding, and blackness and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of blood.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is without force from the nose or ears, or perhaps loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the wound there issues white moisture resembling pus, and also blood as in an open wound;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear to you, desist from the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of a wound when it sinks into the heart are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were pierced into a hard object, and not hollow;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and if it affects the brain, it silences it like the hair, and black blood comes out, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then know without doubt that death ensues.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never leaves the lung is that without pain foam comes from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow hits in the covering of the foot, it is between the small ribs; and there is great swelling and great pain and breathing; and all the limbs move from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow hits the stomach, perhaps something undigested will jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow hits the belly, and nothing comes out of the bowel but feces, then there is no hope for a cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow hits the bladder, and urine comes out and escapes, and the patient feels great pain, know that this wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and armpit and spine of the back and hip and thigh and leg, and similar limbs, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and is not venomous, as I will tell you so that you can do likewise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a certain man that an arrow struck him in the jaw near the ear:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I probed it and dislodged it from under the ear lobe, and he was healed without any numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I extracted an arrow that had struck him under the eyelid, below the eyeball:
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was drawn back, but its tip reached only as far as the shaft.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was great, from a Turkish bow, to all .I. light metal ears; the game was healthy, and no bad incidents came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And he shot an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	The game was healthy; it was a great discomfort to the Christians. I cut off the beards, and made it subtle until I took it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And he drew an arrow out of a man who had it lodged in his head or belly, and I thought he was going to die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after thirty days, his condition did not improve;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and extracted it, and he had no ill effects.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man with an arrow stuck in his back, and the wound is sewn up on top;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and keeps the arrow inside him, and does not change his natural dispositions,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and finds no harm in any of his natural actions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And you will see another man who got an arrow in his face and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and stayed like that without experiencing great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And drew an arrow from the head of one of the king's men who had it lodged in his brain,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly bent to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to attend the wound after it had been treated for four days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I probed it with a thin needle and felt nothing;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pricking and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I placed a cooling and digestive plaster on the area, because the ears were swollen;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the place where the arrow had hit.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the ointment many times, and the wound healed directly, and the patient suffered for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied medicine with a corrosive agent to the wound many times until it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I probed it and felt the tip of the arrow which stuck out in the middle;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I applied the medicine to the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow appeared visibly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it passed well within four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I lanced the wound that I had probed with tweezers, and it would not drain;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	therefore I did not cease from subtlety and cunning with instruments, until I took it on the first day with well-made tweezers,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to what form it will come out at the end of this chapter, as I have experienced it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctors judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it therefore, and the wound was sewed up and the patient completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you about the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you apply your treatment to what I do not say, because books cannot understand everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise teacher considers well very little, and what is present and lacking to him,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	discovers new remedies and instruments, and the descending of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows grow in the members where they are lodged in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out through where it entered is an arrow entering their flesh, and sometimes jumps out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump out now, then leave it as long as the flesh around it becomes putrid and the exit wound heals.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it's lodged in the bone and can't be removed, then leave it for several days, moving it slightly each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps; and if it does not jump, then pierce around with a very fine needle until the hole is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow has pierced into the bone of the skull, and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have mentioned are apparent in the patient: then do not pull it out, but let it be until it is even after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes just to the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not reach the sinus,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient stays for some days without any bad effects, then use the device to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stuck deeply and cannot be removed, then administer cauterization around it, as I have told you; then clean the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged deep within the body and cannot be seen, then cut it off at the tip;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then draw it with an appropriate instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein in the way, then open it as widely as possible;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if the arrow has barbs that are holding it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if you can, remove the arrow that is stuck in two parts at the wound.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or fold the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully so that you do not break the arrow as you pull it out more forcefully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot remove it in one go, then leave it until the flesh around it is swollen, and then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding makes it worse, then administer what we have said about its treatment in that chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of cutting into the nerve and opening a vein, and use every means you can to pull out the arrow without danger,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and position the patient according to how they were when the arrow struck them,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for that is the greatest help, and if you cannot, then position him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	Arrows that come from elsewhere, or where something is seen or felt protruding from them, or the skin is swollen in that area:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Then cut above it, as high as the tweezers can reach, and then pull it out; if it does not come out at once,
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is caught in the bone, then rotate your hand rapidly, so that it goes into the bone and widens the opening, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be extracted, then leave it for now, and then try again to extract it until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is an arrow in it, then it is stuffed with everything.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the shaft is broken, and you see to administer a bandage, then it administers an instrument that is chewed,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow goes into the gum of the instrument; and then it fills up
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is chewed, then it puts an instrument with a point entering in, to ease extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is touched, you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, as much as you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then clean the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits in the buttocks, or the abdomen, or the bladder, or the ribs, and it is superficial, and you can cut over it, then cut over it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut into the vein and the nerve, and then pull it out, and then sew up the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of tweezers used to treat arrows are similar to an owl's beak, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the tip that grabs is also like an owl's beak:
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push out at the tip of the arrow, as is its shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of tweezers to pull and to check if it is there:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common body veins
